<div id="review_1383567982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383567982" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1383567982?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447238355" href="/book/show/26450787-furiously-happy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=feelgood-wholesome">feelgood-wholesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1383567982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14898445381708103421"><blockquote>
  <i>"There will be moments when you have to act like a grown-up. Those moments are tricks. Do not fall for them."</i>
</blockquote><br/>I won’t say too much about <i>Furiously Happy</i>, because I really think the element of surprise is one of the best things about the book. Most of the stories in this book are downright bizarre, and on more than one occasion I thought to myself, “There is no way that actually happened”, and then BOOM, the author provides photographic evidence, and blew my mind once again.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>"[...] my friend</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText14898445381708103421" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"There will be moments when you have to act like a grown-up. Those moments are tricks. Do not fall for them."</i>
</blockquote><br />I won’t say too much about <i>Furiously Happy</i>, because I really think the element of surprise is one of the best things about the book. Most of the stories in this book are downright bizarre, and on more than one occasion I thought to myself, “There is no way that actually happened”, and then BOOM, the author provides photographic evidence, and blew my mind once again.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"[...] my friend Laura asked if I'd come with her on a trip sponsored by the People Who Want You to Go to Australia. I said no because I'm the only person in the world who hates to travel, and because I knew that everything in Australia wants to kill you as violently and painfully as possible."</i>
</blockquote><br />Not only does the author wonderfully explain what it’s like to live with mental illness, but she also makes you laugh about it, which is something we all need to do – take life a little less seriously. On top of that, you get amazing stories about cuddling koalas in a koala suit, taxidermied raccoons, a shitload of possums, and lots of other things you never thought you’d read.<br /><blockquote><i>"As the doctor walked me out he told me to 'stop worrying so much' [...] and I made a note to tell my shrink the breaking news that the medical world finally found the cure for my severe anxiety disorder and that the prescription is 'Just stop worrying so much'.<br /></i>My God<i>, we've come so far with science."</i></blockquote><br />Without a doubt, one of the best books I’ve read this year. Jenny Lawson is a person to watch out for – not only because she’s slightly crazy and lots of weird things happen around her, but also because she is incredibly funny and amazing in every single way. She’s relatable in her social awkwardness and not so relatable in her being stalked by swans, but it’s all part of the magic.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I am privileged to be able to recognise that the sound of laughter is a blessing and a song, to realise that the bright hours spent with my family and friends are extraordinary treasures to be saved, [...]. Those moments are a promise that life is worth fighting for, and that promise is what pulls me through when depression distorts reality and tries to convince me otherwise."</i>
</blockquote><br />For the love of Rory the raccoon, pick up this book. You will not regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14898445381708103421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2120478693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120478693" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120478693?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447238355" href="/book/show/26450787-furiously-happy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120478693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8432460151942129489">This book was really enjoyable! I started it as a physical book and thought it was great, and I finished it with the audiobook and liked that as well! Some of these stories were SO powerful and well-written, and I was underlining them like crazy. It's such a candid and unfiltered book about the experience of mental illness, and I could relate so much to parts of this. However, in the middle of the book, Jenny starts getting really off-topic and just begins telling random funny stories. Don't get</span>
  <span id="freeText8432460151942129489" style="display:none">This book was really enjoyable! I started it as a physical book and thought it was great, and I finished it with the audiobook and liked that as well! Some of these stories were SO powerful and well-written, and I was underlining them like crazy. It's such a candid and unfiltered book about the experience of mental illness, and I could relate so much to parts of this. However, in the middle of the book, Jenny starts getting really off-topic and just begins telling random funny stories. Don't get me wrong, they were enjoyable, but I was left wondering how it related to mental health or her policy of being furiously happy. Other than that, sometimes her jokes were a little bit too lame and she came off as an annoying person in her attempt to be super hilarious all the time, but her writing really reminded me of Mindy Kaling's, and I enjoyed her books as well.<br /><br />This is definitely something that will stick with me even though it wasn't perfect. It spoke true to the experience of debilitating mental illness and how recovery is possible and always something to look forward to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8432460151942129489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9575897425002019266">I don't want to put others off this book because even though it wasn't for me, it may be just the thing for another person. Despite living with depression, something I work on every day to keep in it's place (don't know how else to describe my personal struggle with it) and doing a pretty good job most of the time, I wasn't able to connect with the author's experiences that she relates in the book. We all have our own journey and she makes that very clear in her intro. <br/><br/>My brain just rebelled aga</span>
  <span id="freeText9575897425002019266" style="display:none">I don't want to put others off this book because even though it wasn't for me, it may be just the thing for another person. Despite living with depression, something I work on every day to keep in it's place (don't know how else to describe my personal struggle with it) and doing a pretty good job most of the time, I wasn't able to connect with the author's experiences that she relates in the book. We all have our own journey and she makes that very clear in her intro. <br /><br />My brain just rebelled against the written words...maybe it was the stuffed raccoons...I don't know. She has cats and I love them. I'm usually so much more flexible about books I read but this just hit me as a big NO! I really had this book sitting on my desk, waiting to be picked up and read, for almost a month so I know I was having a problem with it before I even got very far into it. Your mileage may vary. I hate writing non positive reviews but I must admit, I already feel better for having written this one. :-)</span>

<div id="review_1401841872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1401841872" />
    <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader"><img alt="Heidi The Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593309467p2/7986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1401841872?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=bloggers">bloggers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=libraryreads">libraryreads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1401841872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7177638710563193614">Jenny Lawson may not appeal to all readers, but I love her stuff. Her books are like open diaries and sometimes you just have to look away, but I always find myself looking back. I loved her first book and this one was even better. <br/><br/>In addition to being, in my opinion, uproariously funny, Jenny is a poster child for the millions who suffer silently from mental illness and the social stigma that goes along with that. She has more than embraced her condition, she's transcended it into a weird alter</span>
  <span id="freeText7177638710563193614" style="display:none">Jenny Lawson may not appeal to all readers, but I love her stuff. Her books are like open diaries and sometimes you just have to look away, but I always find myself looking back. I loved her first book and this one was even better. <br /><br />In addition to being, in my opinion, uproariously funny, Jenny is a poster child for the millions who suffer silently from mental illness and the social stigma that goes along with that. She has more than embraced her condition, she's transcended it into a weird alternate reality with grinning, taxidermied raccoons and brown (not white) Pegasuses with back herpes.<br /><br />Though she obviously has her dark moments, Jenny's world seems a lot more fun than the ordinary world. That in itself is miraculous when you consider the sheer amount of mental anguish that she's lived through. I think Jenny gives people with debilitating mental illnesses hope- that they too can live a life filled with laughter, quirkiness and fun despite any obstacles.<br /><br />It's weird but my favorite part was the bit about Japanese toilets. I googled it and found out that Japanese toilets are a for-real "thing"- those buttons, squirting water and all. So, in addition to being entertaining and inspiring, this book could also be considered educational. :)<br /><br />If you enjoyed <i>Furiously Happy</i>, you may want to try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26890698.I_m_Just_a_Person" title="I'm Just a Person by Tig Notaro" rel="nofollow noopener">I'm Just a Person</a> by Tig Notaro, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17345259.Mother__Wife__Sister__Human__Warrior__Falcon__Yardstick__Turban__Cabbage_" title="Mother. Wife. Sister. Human. Warrior. Falcon. Yardstick. Turban. Cabbage. by Rob Delaney" rel="nofollow noopener">Mother. Wife. Sister. Human. Warrior. Falcon. Yardstick. Turban. Cabbage.</a> by Rob Delaney or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7775841.Sleepwalk_With_Me_and_Other_Painfully_True_Stories" title="Sleepwalk With Me and Other Painfully True Stories by Mike Birbiglia" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleepwalk With Me and Other Painfully True Stories</a> by Mike Birbiglia.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7177638710563193614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a title="Ashley DiNorcia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley DiNorcia" href="/user/show/3764614-ashley-dinorcia">Ashley DiNorcia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3764614-ashley-dinorcia?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243455452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8036898217058107918">When my husband found out this book was coming out he says <br/>"Is that by the same person who wrote that book you sat on the couch laughing while reading?"<br/>"Yes, yes it is."<br/>"Ugh."<br/><br/><br/>Much to his pleasure, this book had the same effect. He's the Victor of my world but I suspect if a third book rolls around he'll make me vacate the room and read it elsewhere. I truly have never laughed so much while reading as I have while reading both of her books. <br/><br/>Jenny is a magical unicorn of a human and I strongly enc</span>
  <span id="freeText8036898217058107918" style="display:none">When my husband found out this book was coming out he says <br />"Is that by the same person who wrote that book you sat on the couch laughing while reading?"<br />"Yes, yes it is."<br />"Ugh."<br /><br /><br />Much to his pleasure, this book had the same effect. He's the Victor of my world but I suspect if a third book rolls around he'll make me vacate the room and read it elsewhere. I truly have never laughed so much while reading as I have while reading both of her books. <br /><br />Jenny is a magical unicorn of a human and I strongly encourage you read her books. If you or someone you know struggles with mental illness, if you just want to giggle, or if you're a grumpy tightwad who maybe just needs to lighten up a little this book is for you. <br /><br />But also read her first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12868761.Let_s_Pretend_This_Never_Happened_A_Mostly_True_Memoir" title="Let's Pretend This Never Happened A Mostly True Memoir by Jenny Lawson" rel="nofollow noopener">Let's Pretend This Never Happened: A Mostly True Memoir</a> because it's also great and there's some hilarious shit in there and some references you'd probably not want to miss. And her blog. Cause that's where it all started, and where it continues to be awesome in between books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8036898217058107918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13609218520478306931">Furiously Happy: A Funny Book About Horrible Things, Jenny Lawson<br/>The title refers to Lawson's philosophy of being "furiously happy" after becoming so depressed that she eventually decided to force herself to be happy out of frustration and spite, driving herself to adventures and experiences in order to build happy memories to sustain her through bouts of depression. This propels her to do such things as travel to Australia in order to hug a koala while wearing a koala suit, to wear a fancy ball</span>
  <span id="freeText13609218520478306931" style="display:none">Furiously Happy: A Funny Book About Horrible Things, Jenny Lawson<br />The title refers to Lawson's philosophy of being "furiously happy" after becoming so depressed that she eventually decided to force herself to be happy out of frustration and spite, driving herself to adventures and experiences in order to build happy memories to sustain her through bouts of depression. This propels her to do such things as travel to Australia in order to hug a koala while wearing a koala suit, to wear a fancy ballgown on ordinary occasions in order to feel beautiful, and to connect with people in the real world in spite of painful physical ability and severe social anxiety. She also related experiences of other mentally ill people who have gone on their own adventures after being inspired by her. Lawson's memoir also discusses the real challenges of mental illness, such as anxiety and depression. She fully puts these terms into perspective and the daily struggles one might face. One example of her realness is by explaining the physical and mental pain of public appearances such as book signings.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش نسخه اصلی: یادم نیست نسخه ی کتاب در کامپیوتری دیگر است<br />عنوان: شادی از سر خشم : کتاب بامزه‌ ای درباره‌ ی چیزهای وحشتناک؛ نویسنده: جنی لاوسن؛ مترجم: فاطمه جابیک؛ تهران: انتشارات میلکان‏‫، 1397؛ در 320 ص؛ شابک: 9786007443385؛ در 320 ص؛ شابک: 9786007443385؛ موضوع: شوخیها و بذله گوییها از نویسندگان ایالات متحده آمریکا - سده 21 م<br />‬ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1468593464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1468593464" />
    <a title="Derek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13257456-derek"><img alt="Derek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348963993p2/13257456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1468593464?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Derek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Derek" href="/user/show/13257456-derek">Derek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1468593464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17304785174718407395">I'm sorry that Jenny Lawson got dealt a bad hand in life, but honestly, she is a terrible writer. This book is filled with completely uninteresting anecdotes about falling asleep on her arms and them going numb that I thought would somehow tie into her daily struggle. but no that was it. Hilarious. There are several one-liners that would be cute little twitter posts, but listed out in a book is simply tedious. Moreover, the insights into mental illness are so superficial that only people who are</span>
  <span id="freeText17304785174718407395" style="display:none">I'm sorry that Jenny Lawson got dealt a bad hand in life, but honestly, she is a terrible writer. This book is filled with completely uninteresting anecdotes about falling asleep on her arms and them going numb that I thought would somehow tie into her daily struggle. but no that was it. Hilarious. There are several one-liners that would be cute little twitter posts, but listed out in a book is simply tedious. Moreover, the insights into mental illness are so superficial that only people who are dealing with something similar would appreciate, but it doesn't provide much for people on the outside to grasp to make sense of the world these people inhabit. The section on self-harming was pretty serious, but I didn't get anything from it other than it sucks. <br /><br />But the most severe crime which made the book un-finish-able for me is that it isn't funny whatsoever. The jokes are clumsy and obvious, the pop culture references forced, and the "wackiness" is just annoying. Ultimately, a lot of the book feels like a cross between a pitch session for a terrible sitcom and someone's therapy journal that hasn't seen any kind of revising or editing. Moreover, she seems almost proud of the fact that she's perfectly content to not do any work and just pump out writing whenever she feels like it. It proves to be a thesis statement for the book itself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17304785174718407395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I have anxiety, and although my experiences and disorders aren't the same as Jenny's I found myself relating to the fears and emotion behind nearly all of the situations she described.   <span id="freeText13125230794850610665" style="display:none">So good. Listened to the audiobook, which was narrated by Jenny herself.<br /><br />Jenny talks candidly (and hilariously!) about her life and mental illnesses. I have anxiety, and although my experiences and disorders aren't the same as Jenny's I found myself relating to the fears and emotion behind nearly all of the situations she described. Her stories are outrageous and sometimes awful, but she always makes sure you know YOU AREN'T ALONE. I feel like I could listen to this audiobook forever and still get something out of it each time. I need the constant reminder that it's ok to be afraid, to be different, to be sensitive to things other people can't understand.<br /><br />I'd absolutely recommend this to anyone. You will either find solace or insight about mental illness, and undoubtedly a good laugh too.</span>

    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475256742p2/41788446.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1402168248?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/41788446-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788446-hannah?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1402168248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12533934507156096778">I adore Jenny Lawson and her wit and humanity and bravery and just sheer weirdness. <br/><br/>This was one of the first memoirs I read when I decided to read more non-fiction (which by the way, brilliant decision on my end) and when I needed something fun and quick to read on my flight from hell back from holiday (I just have the worst luck when it comes to flying, but this time really took the cake) this seemed like the obvious pick. And I am so glad to have decided to re-read this. Jenny Lawson is an ab</span>
  <span id="freeText12533934507156096778" style="display:none">I adore Jenny Lawson and her wit and humanity and bravery and just sheer weirdness. <br /><br />This was one of the first memoirs I read when I decided to read more non-fiction (which by the way, brilliant decision on my end) and when I needed something fun and quick to read on my flight from hell back from holiday (I just have the worst luck when it comes to flying, but this time really took the cake) this seemed like the obvious pick. And I am so glad to have decided to re-read this. Jenny Lawson is an absolute hero - and beyond hilarious. I have so much respect for her honesty and her vulnerability and her bravery, but its her wit that lifts this beyond many of the other memoirs I have read since reading this.<br /><br />Jenny Lawson is painfully honest about her struggle with mental illness - and the picture she paints s not pretty. I have so much respect for the fact that she gets up time and time again and that she found a way to deal with her illness. I cannot even image how hard that must be at times. I adore her manifesto of living "furiously happy" and I adore the strength she shows. <br /><br />This time around I also really appreciated her relationship with her husband a lot more than the last time - he is the straight man to her weirdness and the picture it paints of their relationship is just beautiful. I love when people are happy with their spouses.<br /><br />So, yes, brilliantly done memoir with humour and wit but also raw and honest pain. Which seems to be just my favourite type of memoir (not sure what that says about me). Also, she makes taxidermy sound a lot more fun than I thought possible.<br /><br />First sentence: "Dear reader, Right now you're holding this book in your hands and wondering if it's worth reading."</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1958804021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1958804021" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1958804021?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1958804021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13131694687191507575"><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Jenny Lawson - born and raised in Texas - is a journalist, blogger, author, and humorist who suffers from mental illness. Lawson describes herself as having clinical depression, severe anxiety disorder, impulse control disorder, avoidance personality disorder, and depersonalization disorder (which makes her feel detached from reality). She also has rheumatoid arthritis, autoimmune problems, self-harm issues, trichotillomania (she pulls out her hair), mild obsessive compulsive disorder, </span>
  <span id="freeText13131694687191507575" style="display:none"><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Jenny Lawson - born and raised in Texas - is a journalist, blogger, author, and humorist who suffers from mental illness. Lawson describes herself as having clinical depression, severe anxiety disorder, impulse control disorder, avoidance personality disorder, and depersonalization disorder (which makes her feel detached from reality). She also has rheumatoid arthritis, autoimmune problems, self-harm issues, trichotillomania (she pulls out her hair), mild obsessive compulsive disorder, and panic attacks. This makes Lawson's life challenging but - in spite of it all - she's a very funny lady! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070458i/27057562.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <b>Jenny Lawson</b><br><br>This is Lawson's second book and, like the first, it provides encouragement to people with mental health issues.....and to everyone else whose life isn't perfect. Lawson's motivational observations are scattered among many amusing anecdotes that make gentle fun of everything and everyone, including herself. <br><br>Lawson describes one of her troubling behaviors as follows: She was in the bathroom, blood flowing from the scratches on her head that she'd made with her nails. Lawson describes how this made her feel: "The pressure in my head was gone. The pain in me was floating away. Panic was fading slowly." In short, the physical pain distracted from the mental pain. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070458i/27057566.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For Lawson, these kinds of self-destructive actions led to behavioral therapy, various medications, learning to redirect her thoughts, snapping rubber bands on her wrist, and squeezing ice until her hands burned. Lawson's basic philosophy - reiterated in different ways throughout the book - is: "Without the dark there isn't light, without pain there isn't relief." <br><br>In spite of these low periods Lawson has the gift of seeing (and creating) the funny all around her. For instance:<br><br>Lawson is picking up her meds at a Texas pharmacy and sees a box of Milk Bone dog biscuits beside the cash register. She thinks maybe someone returned them until - while ringing her up - the pharmacist casually reaches into the box and scarfs down some broken biscuits. Lawson is aghast, wondering if she's high....or if Milk Bones are actually delicious and the pharmacist is a genius who discovered really cheap cookies. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070458i/27057570.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lawson loves her stuffed raccoon, Rory. Rory is posed standing up on his hind legs with his arms stretched wide and a huge smile on his face (see book cover). Late one night Lawson decides Rory should ride, rodeo style, on her cats - Ferris Mewler, Hunter S. Tomcat, and Rolly - for a photo montage. So Lawson tries to mount Rory on the kitties, who flop over before she can get the shot, "like a bunch of ingrates that don't understand art." At one point, Lawson's husband Victor, woken by the racket at 2 A.M., peeks out of the bedroom just as Ferris Mewler is streaking across the room with Rory on board. "What the hell is that?" cries Victor. (Can you imagine? LOL)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550071038i/27057655.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070458i/27057567.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Speaking of cats, Lawson thinks an awesome name for a cat would be "The President" because you'd find yourself saying things like: The President will not stop sitting on my keyboard; The President just threw up on the new rug; I love sleeping with The President. When Lawson mentioned this to Victor, he yelled "You can't have any more cats. I have to clean up after them. And I'll be damned if I have to scoop The President's shit too." (ha ha ha).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070458i/27057565.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For Lawson, one of the difficulties of being a successful author is the inevitable promotional tour and attendant parties. Lawson gets so anxious at events like these that she sometimes hides behind the podium, cowers under a table, or takes shelter in the bathroom.....and occasionally she can't leave her hotel room at all. At one stop, in the Tenderloin District of San Francisco, the crowded streets forced Lawson to stay in her room and - lacking room service - eat peanut butter crackers (that she'd brought along) for days. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070458i/27057561.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For her last book tour Lawson had to fly constantly. According to the author, "it really fucked with my anxiety disorder to the point where I had a mild nervous breakdown." Lawson's shrink advised her to get a service animal, which provides support to people with these difficulties. Lawson thought of training Ferris Mewler, but his explosive diarrhea during trips put him out of the running. So Lawson looked into other animals, including a pony. She notes, "Pony Danza would make a great support animal on a plane.....but Victor got all shitty about having an indoor pony pet." (Lawson's a genius at naming animals! )<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550071935i/27057701.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Lawson counsels the reader that, "Even when everything's going your way you can still be sad, or anxious, or numb.....because you can't always control your brain or your emotions. It's terrifying but you learn that it's okay to prefer your idea of heaven - like live tweeting zombie movies from under a blanket of kittens - rather than someone else's idea, like fame, fortune, or parties." She advises, "Appreciate the unique moments that recharge you. I want banana popsicles dipped in Malibu rum." (Sounds good to me!)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070682i/27057612.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>In one entry, Lawson lists things she may have accidently blurted out during uncomfortable silences at her psychiatrist's office:<br>"I need to find a skilled arsonist, not necessarily to burn anything down. I just want to have the option. I need an arsonist on retainer. I'm pretty sure that's legal as long as I don't use it."<br>"My primary thoughts during holidays are stab stab stab, run away."<br>"I hate it when it's too hot for a blanket because I have this phobia that I'll float up to the ceiling without it and then I'll get chopped up by the ceiling fan."<br>"On the way here I saw a cloud that looked like a skull and my first thought, Death Eaters."<br> Of course the psychiatrist just responds, " How does that make you feel? Tell me more."<br> <br>In one funny anecdote Lawson talks about a visit to her beauty salon. The beautician suggests, "We should get you a Brazilian blowout. It's not bad. You just have to be extra careful for the first day or two. You can't put your hair in a ponytail or anything, or it could compromise the treatment." To which Lawson responds, "What the shit. Who puts their pubic hair in a ponytail?" And the beautician explains that this is a blow drying treatment for the hair on your head - that straightens it out and makes it less frizzy. "Ohhhh...Yeahhhhh" responds a sheepish Lawson. :) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070682i/27057613.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In another wry entry Lawson talks about moving into a new house, chosen in part, because of the safe area. "The house seemed perfect..... the gated community seemed perfect." However, in short order: Lawson got attacked by swans at the local pond; a man in the neighborhood had a full on shoot out with the police in his driveway (and got arrested); and a flyer was circulated saying that a cougar had come down from the mountain nearby and eaten a lady's dog WHILE SHE WAS WALKING IT! Lawson notes, "I just assume the sewers are filled with panthers because this seems to be the direction things are taking."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550070458i/27057563.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lawson also describes a trip to Japan with Victor, where a small gang broke into their hotel room (a misunderstanding); and a journey to Australia with a friend - where she wanted to hug a koala while she was dressed as a koala, and tried to see a kangaroo's three vaginas (these is a real thing, but not visible on the outside). <br><br>The writer also describes more of her mental health battles, in an effort to give hope to people who struggle along with her. Lawson's message comes across loud and clear: 'you can go on; you can make it; medication helps; twitter (where lots of 'nuts' hang out) helps; the bad times will pass'..... and so on. 'Just hang in there and appreciate the good times.' The author expresses deep appreciation to her fans, and is profoundly touched by messages from troubled souls who have been brought back from the brink by her writing. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550086645i/27058667.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>On the downside, the book's humor is a little uneven, and some stories fall flat or feel forced, as if Lawson engaged in an activity just to have something to write about (and it didn't turn out to be that hilarious). <br><br>I'd recommend the book to anyone who wants a laugh or needs a boost on occasion (which, I suspect, is everyone). I listened to the audio version, narrated by the author, and was treated to a 'bonus chapter.' So consider getting that version if you can. <br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13131694687191507575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1892312084" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1892312084?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1892312084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17298217982811272514">There's nothing wrong with being optimistic or looking at the bright side of things, but I don't know about this book... I didn't necessarily dislike it, it was alright, I guess. But I don't like books about mental illnesses or books that try to find humor in situations that, no matter which way you spin it, just aren't funny. It reminded me of an Augusten Burroughs book, the type of humor that just seems forced and false more than anything else.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2863585104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2863585104" />
    <a title="Ines" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43642795-ines"><img alt="Ines" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542692123p2/43642795.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2863585104?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ines" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ines" href="/user/show/43642795-ines">Ines</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2863585104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8241080829538663690">Never laughed so hard reading a series of exagerations and suspicious fibs as you will find them exposed here.... What people won’t do for money...wow... I should get published all the crazy that comes out of the mouths of my actually “crazy" patients. Silly me, we really could have made a lot of money in the institution where I work..... and then rearrange things, create new monitored housing, buy new materials, invite new specialists to develop new rehabilitative therapies.... Shame on us who </span>
  <span id="freeText8241080829538663690" style="display:none">Never laughed so hard reading a series of exagerations and suspicious fibs as you will find them exposed here.... What people won’t do for money...wow... I should get published all the crazy that comes out of the mouths of my actually “crazy" patients. Silly me, we really could have made a lot of money in the institution where I work..... and then rearrange things, create new monitored housing, buy new materials, invite new specialists to develop new rehabilitative therapies.... Shame on us who were born in Italy, brought up to think that certain things are not to be done or even thought about, slaves of the concept "no to the exploitation of the misfortunes of others.. <br />A concentration of exagerated nonsenses I thought I couldn’t read them by Americans, I’m not saying they don’t make you laugh...... but wow, this chick will be a cronic bipolar but not stupid...<br /> this "marketing" depression was worth it!!! ( i bet it really!!)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />."Hahahahahah!!! penso di non aver mai riso cosi tanto leggendo una serie di fregnacce e balle a raffica come le troverete esposte qui dentro....<br />Cosa non si fa per soldi, caspiterina, dovrei far pubblicare tutte le pazzie e le follie che escono dalla bocca dei miei pazienti veramente "matti".<br />Vedete come siamo scemi nell'istituto dove lavoro.....avremo potuto fare soldi a palate, indi risistemare un sacco di cose, creare nuovi alloggi abitativi monitorati, nuovo materiale, invitare nuovi specialisti per creare nuovi percorsi riabilitativi....<br />Mannaggia a noi che nati in Italia, e tutti cresciuti che certe cose non si fanno e neanche si pensano, schiavi del concetto "no allo sfruttamento delle disgrazie altrui..."<br />Un concentrato di assurdità in salsa pecoreccia pensavo di non poterle leggere per bocca di americani, non dico che non facciano ridere...... ma caspita, sta tipa sarà psicotica ma mica scema...<br />viva la commercializzazione (monetizzazione) della depressione!!! e un brindisi ai suoi soldi buoni.</span>

		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('No+ykRywBkXEm66QTSooxlCaTcmhGf3PZGZLC6ONcz2x8sURcG1CeQ0wmllDEO4UFsHN8lZioYGaCJwRP1pIaQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0Zkd/UaxB4ea/A3W+YhyrlkuzUB6w1lrYL+DwyU19BhW5Gp9KmxDu1NXOR/3srR8H3VNe424BSWe0VTZueLPTA==')})
  }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/43075476-furiously-happy">Quotes from Furiously Happy: ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;When you come out of the grips of a depression there is an incredible relief, but not one you feel allowed to celebrate. Instead, the feeling of victory is replaced with anxiety that it will happen again, and with shame and vulnerability when you see how your illness affected your family, your work, everything left untouched while you struggled to survive. We come back to life thinner, paler, weaker … but as survivors. Survivors who don’t get pats on the back from coworkers who congratulate them on making it. Survivors who wake to more work than before because their friends and family are exhausted from helping them fight a battle they may not even understand. I hope to one day see a sea of people all wearing silver ribbons as a sign that they understand the secret battle, and as a celebration of the victories made each day as we individually pull ourselves up out of our foxholes to see our scars heal, and to remember what the sun looks like.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7282065-when-you-come-out-of-the-grips-of-a-depression">456 likes</a>

          </div>
